+# Multi-Engine SEO and AI Search Report for a Foreign-Tourist-to-China Website, 2025-2026
+
+Target site type: a new travel site helping foreign visitors plan, enter, pay, move around, and solve practical problems in China.
+
+Bottom line: optimize first for Google because it still owns roughly 90% of global traditional search share, but do not treat "Google SEO" as the whole discovery system. A China-travel site also needs Bing/IndexNow coverage, Russian/Yandex coverage, Korean/Naver coverage, selective Baidu coverage, and AI-search citation readiness.
+
+## Executive Findings
+
+1. Google remains the primary acquisition engine for most foreign travelers outside China, but AI Overviews and AI Mode have changed the value of informational travel pages: generic destination summaries are easier for Google to answer directly, while original, current, practical pages are more likely to win clicks and citations.
+2. The March 2024 Google core/spam changes matter in 2025-2026 because "helpful content" is no longer a separate periodic system; it is part of core ranking. Thin "10 things to do in Shanghai" pages are a weak launch asset unless they contain firsthand value, current constraints, and unique evidence.
+3. Core Web Vitals now use INP instead of FID. For a travel site, the practical risk is not only ranking; it is losing mobile users who are trying to read maps, payment steps, transit instructions, or visa rules on slow hotel/cellular connections.
+4. MUM, RankBrain, BERT, and related Google language systems are not knobs to optimize directly. They reward complete intent coverage: synonyms, entities, transliterated place names, Chinese names, local constraints, and answer-level clarity.
+5. Bing is a must-submit engine even if its raw share is much smaller than Google's because Bing powers or heavily influences Bing Copilot, DuckDuckGo traditional links, Yahoo, Microsoft surfaces, and at least some ChatGPT Search contexts.
+6. IndexNow is the fastest indexing lever outside Google. Use it for new, updated, and deleted URLs, especially pages whose usefulness decays quickly: visa-free policies, attraction reservation rules, payment app setup, train ticket instructions, holiday closures, and seasonal events.
+7. DuckDuckGo has no meaningful standalone webmaster workflow. Traditional result visibility mostly flows through Bing, while Instant Answers and special modules come from DuckDuckGo's own crawler/indexes and specialty sources.
+8. Yandex is relevant for Russian-speaking travelers to China, especially as Russia-China travel flows and visa-free/group travel interest grow. Russian pages must be native Cyrillic content, not English pages machine-translated at scale.
+9. Naver is the most non-Google special case. For Korean travelers, an external Korean website alone is not enough because Naver search heavily surfaces Naver Blog, Cafe, Knowledge iN, and other internal content blocks.
+10. Korean-language content is worth doing. South Korea is a major China inbound source market, and 2025 reporting showed a strong rebound in South Korean travel to China after visa-free policy expansion.
+11. Baidu is strategically optional for this site. It is not important for most foreign travelers before they arrive in China, but it can matter for Chinese-language pages and for some travelers searching during their stay.
+12. Do not delay a global launch for Baidu. The account, verification, language, hosting, compliance, and ICP-related friction is disproportionate unless the site has a Chinese-language acquisition plan.
+13. ChatGPT Search is now a real referral and citation surface. Allow `OAI-SearchBot`; it is separate from `GPTBot`, which is the training crawler.
+14. Perplexity is built around citations and real-time retrieval. It should be treated as a citation engine: clear answer blocks, authoritative sourcing, and bot accessibility matter.
+15. Bing Copilot citations depend on Bing discovery and ranking. Bing Webmaster Tools plus IndexNow is the foundation.
+16. Google AI Overviews use Google's index and ranking systems, but source selection is not identical to normal organic ranking. Traditional SEO remains necessary but not sufficient.
+17. AI search engines prefer content that is easy to quote, verify, and segment. Pages should include concise answer paragraphs, tables, current dates, official-source citations, and original observations.
+18. Schema helps machines disambiguate entities and page types, but schema alone will not make a page citable. The page itself must contain extractable facts.
+19. For multilingual SEO, use subdirectories on one strong domain at launch: `/en/`, `/zh-hans/`, `/es/`, `/fr/`, `/de/`, `/ja/`, `/ko/`, `/ru/`.
+20. Every localized URL needs reciprocal `hreflang`, a self-reference, and `x-default`; the canonical should point to the same-language canonical URL, not to English.
+21. Do not auto-redirect crawlers or users by IP/language header. Offer a visible language switcher and let search engines crawl every language URL.
+22. Hosting location is much less important than speed, crawlability, and regional accessibility. For Google, server location is not a clear targeting signal; for users, latency and reliability still matter.
+23. Vercel Edge is a good default for a Next.js/static international site; Cloudflare is stronger for DNS/WAF/cache controls, AI crawler management, and operational visibility. Either can work if bots are not accidentally blocked.
+24. Mainland China performance is a separate project. Vercel states it has no mainland China infrastructure, and China CDN/mainland hosting usually requires ICP filing or a local partner.
+25. The most valuable China-travel pages are not broad inspiration pages; they are "foreign visitor problem" pages: visas, transit without Chinese, payment apps, SIM/eSIM, train tickets, maps, ride-hailing, hotel check-in, airport transfer, toilets, dietary constraints, scams, emergency numbers, and attraction booking.
+26. The site should cite official sources on volatile topics and show "last checked" dates. AI engines and users both need freshness cues for policies that change.
+27. Multilingual expansion should be demand-led: publish English first, then Korean and Russian if resources are limited, then Japanese/Spanish/French/German based on search demand and market data.
+28. Korean and Russian pages need native keyword research and native examples; translating English query structure will miss how travelers actually search.
+29. Measurement must include search-console data, Bing/Yandex/Naver dashboards, referrer logs from AI engines, bot log monitoring, and manual citation tests.
+30. The defensible strategy is "search engine discoverability plus AI-source worthiness": crawlable, fast, canonical, localized pages that contain unique, current, factual travel answers.
+
+## A. Google
+
+### 2025-2026 Changes That Matter
+
+Google is still the default starting point for most foreign travelers. Statcounter reported Google at about 90% worldwide search share in 2025, with Bing, Yandex, Yahoo, DuckDuckGo, and Baidu far behind globally: https://gs.statcounter.com/search-engine-market-share
+
+Google's 2025-2026 SEO baseline for this site:
+
+- Helpful content is part of core ranking. Google's March 2024 core update integrated helpfulness signals into core ranking systems and introduced tougher spam policies for scaled content abuse, expired domain abuse, and site reputation abuse: https://developers.google.com/search/blog/2024/03/core-update-spam-policies
+- Create pages for real traveler tasks, not keyword inventory. Google's helpful-content guidance asks whether content is useful, reliable, people-first, and satisfies a visitor's reason for coming: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/fundamentals/creating-helpful-content
+- AI Overviews and AI Mode are now normal Google Search surfaces. Google says sites appearing in AI features are included in overall Search Console traffic, but there is no separate simple "AI Overview ranking" lever: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/appearance/ai-overviews
+- Core Web Vitals now include INP for responsiveness. For a travel site, optimize interactive maps, accordions, language switchers, image galleries, and route filters so tap response stays fast: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/appearance/core-web-vitals
+- Google's ranking systems guide still describes RankBrain and MUM as AI systems for understanding language, concepts, and complex meaning. That means pages should cover complete intent and related entities rather than repeating exact keywords: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/appearance/ranking-systems-guide
+- Google's current "How Search Works" materials emphasize relevance, usability, expertise of sources, location, language, freshness, and context: https://www.google.com/search/howsearchworks/how-search-works/ranking-results/
+
+### What Changed for Travel Content
+
+Travel planning has shifted from "blue link research" to mixed answer surfaces: AI Overviews, destination modules, map/local packs, travel widgets, videos, forums, Reddit, and OTA results. Generic travel articles are easier for search engines to summarize without sending traffic. The site should therefore publish pages with information engines cannot safely invent:
+
+- exact foreigner workflows: "How to set up Alipay as a US/EU visitor in 2026", "How to buy high-speed rail tickets without a Chinese ID", "How to use Shanghai Metro with foreign cards";
+- original verification: screenshots, tested steps, date-stamped checks, first-hand notes, photos, known failure cases;
+- official citations: immigration, consulates, railway, metro, attraction ticketing, payment providers;
+- structured summaries: answer first, then details, then exceptions;
+- freshness: "Last checked: 2026-05-10" for policy pages and "Updated monthly" for volatile pages.
+
+Recent AI Overview studies point in the same direction. Semrush found AI Overviews expanded materially through 2025, while BrightEdge and seoClarity found that AI Overview citations overlap with organic results but are not identical. For travel, BrightEdge reported low but growing top-10 overlap, which means ranking well helps, but pages also need answer-level precision: https://www.semrush.com/blog/semrush-ai-overviews-study/ and https://www.brightedge.com/resources/weekly-ai-search-insights/ai-overviews-one-year-presence-size-citing and https://www.seoclarity.net/research/ai-overviews-impact
+
+### Search Console Workflow
+
+Set up Google Search Console on day one:
+
+- Add the domain property: https://search.google.com/search-console
+- Submit sitemap index and language-specific sitemaps in the Sitemaps report. Google says the Sitemaps report lets you submit sitemap files and track parsing errors: https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/7451001
+- Use URL Inspection for the homepage, core guides, and new/updated volatile pages. Google says URL Inspection can request indexing, but indexing is not guaranteed and bulk updates should be handled with sitemaps and `lastmod`: https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/9012289
+- Use Performance reports weekly to filter by query, page, country, device, and search appearance. Search Console reports impressions, clicks, CTR, and position: https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/10268906 and https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/7576553
+- Monitor Core Web Vitals after real field data accumulates. A travel site's mobile pages should be under the INP threshold before launch if possible, not after traffic arrives.
+
+### International Targeting in Google
+
+Use Google-supported localized URLs and `hreflang`:
+
+- Each language must have a unique URL.
+- Each page must list every alternate version, including itself.
+- Include `x-default` for the language picker or default global page.
+- Do not use `hreflang` as a ranking boost; it is a version-selection signal.
+- Do not canonicalize all languages to English.
+
+Google's localized-pages documentation covers HTML, HTTP header, and XML sitemap implementations: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/advanced/crawling/localized-versions
+
+Google's multi-regional guide explains URL structure tradeoffs and notes that server location is not a clear geotargeting signal when CDNs are common: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/advanced/crawling/managing-multi-regional-sites
+
+## B. Bing
+
+### Setup
+
+Set up Bing Webmaster Tools immediately after Google:
+
+- Create or sign in to Bing Webmaster Tools and import verified Google Search Console properties where possible.
+- Submit the sitemap index.
+- Use URL Inspection to test crawlability, HTTP status, blocked resources, and indexing status.
+- Use Site Explorer, keyword research, crawl reports, and performance data.
+
+Bing's 2025 Webmaster Tools guidance highlights URL Inspection, sitemap submission through Bing Webmaster Tools or robots.txt, and Google Search Console import: https://blogs.bing.com/webmaster/June-2025/Start-Using-Bing-Webmaster-Tools-to-Improve-Your-Site-Visibility
+
+### How Bing Ranking Differs From Google
+
+Bing's public ranking documentation is more explicit about several signals:
+
+- relevance to the query;
+- quality and credibility;
+- user engagement signals;
+- freshness;
+- location and language;
+- page load time.
+
+Microsoft's "How Bing delivers search results" page was updated in March 2025 and says Bing considers the user's location, page language, where a page is hosted, other visitors' location, freshness, user interaction, and page load time: https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/bing/how-bing-delivers-search-results
+
+Practical implications for a new China-travel site:
+
+- Bing may reward clear titles/H1s and exact topical relevance faster than Google.
+- Keep pages cleanly organized by task and city: `/en/guides/alipay-for-foreigners/`, `/en/shanghai/metro/`, `/ru/visa-free-transit-china/`.
+- Avoid over-templated programmatic city pages unless every page has unique evidence.
+- Submit changes with IndexNow.
+
+### Bing's AI and Distribution Impact
+
+Bing is not only Bing.com. It influences:
+
+- Microsoft Copilot and Copilot Search, which display sources and links: https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/bing/copilot-search
+- Microsoft 365 Copilot web search, which sends generated web queries to Bing when web search is on: https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/topic/how-web-search-works-in-microsoft-365-copilot-chat-and-agents-94c45d32-1a77-4f82-8e05-58dfb9afac48
+- DuckDuckGo traditional web links, which DuckDuckGo says are largely sourced from Bing: https://duckduckgo.com/duckduckgo-help-pages/results/sources
+- Some ChatGPT Search contexts. OpenAI's Enterprise/Edu help says disassociated search queries may be shared with Bing to return web results: https://help.openai.com/en/articles/10093903-chatgpt-search-for-enterprise-and-edu
+
+### IndexNow
+
+Implement IndexNow as a first-class indexing pipeline:
+
+- Generate and host an IndexNow key file.
+- Ping new, updated, and deleted URLs.
+- Send only materially changed URLs, not the whole site every hour.
+- Use it for Bing and Yandex coverage.
+
+Bing's IndexNow setup page: https://www.bing.com/indexnow/getstarted
+
+IndexNow protocol documentation: https://www.indexnow.org/documentation
+
+## C. DuckDuckGo
+
+DuckDuckGo does not provide a Google-Search-Console-style webmaster tool. Its official source page says:
+
+- traditional links and images are largely sourced from Bing;
+- it uses many other sources for Instant Answers;
+- it maintains DuckDuckBot and its own indexes to support results.
+
+Source: https://duckduckgo.com/duckduckgo-help-pages/results/sources
+
+What flows through automatically:
+
+- Bing-indexed pages can appear in DuckDuckGo traditional results.
+- Strong Bing titles/descriptions often influence DuckDuckGo snippets.
+- IndexNow indirectly helps because Bing discovery improves.
+
+What needs separate handling:
+
+- Allow DuckDuckBot in robots.txt and WAF rules.
+- Create clean favicons, Open Graph images, and entity pages.
+- Build presence in trusted sources DuckDuckGo may use for answers: Wikipedia/Wikidata where genuinely notable, official organization profiles, major travel platforms, and structured local listings.
+- Monitor referral logs and manual `site:` checks; there is no DuckDuckGo submission dashboard.
+
+Important nuance: older industry summaries often describe DuckDuckGo as using Bing, Yandex, Yahoo, and many other sources. DuckDuckGo's current official documentation emphasizes Bing, its own crawler/indexes, and specialized sources. For implementation, Bing Webmaster Tools plus open crawler access is the only practical webmaster lever.
+
+## D. Yandex
+
+### Why It Matters
+
+Yandex matters for Russian-speaking travelers and CIS audiences. China-Russia travel has been recovering and policy changes have raised interest in China trips. In 2025, China state media reported rising arrivals from Russia in winter destinations such as Harbin, and Interfax reported Russian tourist trips to China at meaningful scale in Q1 2025: https://english.scio.gov.cn/m/chinavoices/2025-12/19/content_118237101.html and https://interfax.com/newsroom/top-stories/112582/
+
+### Webmaster Setup
+
+Use Yandex Webmaster:
+
+- Add and verify the site.
+- Submit the sitemap.
+- Check robots.txt and site structure.
+- Monitor crawl statistics and indexed pages.
+- Implement IndexNow.
+
+Yandex Webmaster landing page: https://webmaster.yandex.com/
+
+Yandex site-indexing guide: https://yandex.ru/support/webmaster/en/recommendations/indexing
+
+Yandex site verification docs: https://m.yandex.ru/support/webmaster/en/service/rights
+
+Yandex IndexNow support: https://yandex.com/support/webmaster/en/indexing-options/index-now
+
+### Cyrillic Content Optimization
+
+Russian pages should be written for Russian travelers, not translated word-for-word from English:
+
+- Use native Cyrillic headings and queries: "безвизовый транзит в Китае", "как платить в Китае иностранцу", "Alipay для туристов", "поезд в Китае без китайского ID".
+- Include Chinese place names and transliterations where useful: "Шанхай (上海)", "Запретный город / Гугун (故宫)".
+- Use `lang="ru"`, Russian title tags, Russian meta descriptions, and Russian alt text.
+- Add practical constraints Russian travelers search for: UnionPay/Mir payment issues, VPN expectations, cash/card acceptance, Russian-language tours, embassy/consulate links.
+- Earn Russian-language mentions from travel forums, media, bloggers, and Q&A platforms instead of relying only on the English backlink profile.
+
+## E. Naver
+
+### Why It Matters
+
+Korean travelers are a major China inbound audience. SCMP reported roughly 3.16 million South Korean visitors to China in 2025, up 36.9% from 2024, after China extended visa-free access for South Korean passport holders: https://www.scmp.com/news/china/diplomacy/article/3351425/whats-fuelling-surge-south-koreans-travelling-china
+
+Korea's search market is also not Google-like. 2026 reporting from Korea Times and Yonhap cited InternetTrend data showing Naver above 60% search share in South Korea in 2025, with Google second: https://www.koreatimes.co.kr/business/tech-science/20260416/naver-remains-dominant-player-in-koreas-search-market and https://en.yna.co.kr/view/AEN20260104002400320
+
+### Naver Webmaster Setup
+
+Use Naver Search Advisor:
+
+- Register the site.
+- Verify ownership.
+- Submit sitemap/robots.txt information.
+- Make sure Naver's crawler, Yeti, can access the site.
+- Monitor external web search exposure and clicks.
+
+Naver Search Advisor: https://searchadvisor.naver.com/
+
+Naver SEO basic guide: https://searchadvisor.naver.com/guide/seo-help
+
+Naver robots.txt guide: https://searchadvisor.naver.com/guide/seo-basic-robots
+
+Naver exposure/click report docs: https://searchadvisor.naver.com/guide/report-expose-ctr
+
+### Why Naver SEO Is Different
+
+Naver's own documentation notes that Search Advisor exposure/click reporting covers web-search areas and excludes areas such as VIEW and blog search. That is the core strategic issue: Korean users often see Naver Blog, Cafe, Knowledge iN, and platform modules before ordinary external websites.
+
+Recommendation:
+
+- Yes, build Korean-language content, but do not stop at `/ko/` pages.
+- Launch a small Korean content program on Naver Blog around high-intent travel problems.
+- Seed or participate in relevant Naver Cafe discussions where appropriate and non-spammy.
+- Use native Korean titles and search phrasing: "중국 무비자 여행", "상하이 2박3일 코스", "중국 알리페이 외국인 등록", "중국 고속철도 예매", "위챗페이 외국인".
+- Make the external `/ko/` site the canonical, evergreen, cited reference; use Naver Blog/Cafe as discovery and trust surfaces.
+- Include Chinese names beside Korean names for copy/paste into Chinese apps.
+
+## F. Baidu
+
+### Should We Bother?
+
+For this specific business, Baidu is low priority at launch.
+
+Why:
+
+- The primary user is outside China before traveling. They will usually use Google, Bing, Naver, Yandex, DuckDuckGo, YouTube, Reddit, TikTok, Instagram, Trip.com, or local-language search.
+- Baidu is strongest for Chinese-language users inside mainland China, not English-speaking foreign travelers planning from abroad.
+- Baidu registration and ongoing SEO are operationally heavier than Bing/Yandex/Naver.
+- Mainland hosting or China CDN usually requires ICP filing or a local partner; without that, mainland performance and Baidu trust may be weaker.
+
+Why still consider it later:
+
+- Some inbound travelers may search during their stay on Chinese networks.
+- A Simplified Chinese section can help foreign residents, bilingual travelers, overseas Chinese, and people searching Chinese keywords.
+- If the site publishes Chinese-language local guides, Baidu indexing may bring incremental traffic.
+
+Minimum launch posture:
+
+- Do not block Baiduspider unless there is a legal/content reason.
+- Provide a crawlable Simplified Chinese section only if it can be maintained.
+- Do not invest in mainland hosting, ICP, Baidu account operations, Baijiahao, Baike, or Baidu-specific content until global discovery is working.
+
+Baidu official Baiduspider/robots page: https://www.baidu.com/search/robots_english.html
+
+Baidu Search Resource Platform: https://ziyuan.baidu.com/
+
+Recent China-SEO analyses consistently point to the same practical constraints for foreign sites: Chinese-language quality, mainland performance, ICP/hosting friction, and Baidu ecosystem participation. Treat these as a later China-market project, not a blocker for a foreign-tourist site: https://www.chinaseo.com/the-great-digital-wall-deciphering-baidus-treatment-of-foreign-websites-2025-2026-strategy-guide/
+
+## G. AI Search Engines
+
+### ChatGPT Search
+
+OpenAI launched ChatGPT Search on October 31, 2024 and expanded availability through December 2024 and February 2025: https://openai.com/index/introducing-chatgpt-search
+
+OpenAI's help page says ChatGPT Search can automatically search the web, return inline citations, show a source panel, use approximate location for local results, and sometimes work with search partners: https://help.openai.com/en/articles/9237897-chatgpt-search
+
+For publishers, the crawler distinction matters:
+
+- `OAI-SearchBot` is for surfacing websites in ChatGPT search features.
+- `GPTBot` is for crawling content that may be used for training foundation models.
+- `ChatGPT-User` is used for some user-triggered actions and is not the automatic search opt-out mechanism.
+
+OpenAI crawler docs: https://platform.openai.com/docs/bots
+
+OpenAI publisher FAQ: https://help.openai.com/en/articles/12627856-publishers-and-developers-faq
+
+Recommendation:
+
+- Allow `OAI-SearchBot`.
+- Allow `ChatGPT-User` at the WAF/network layer where possible.
+- Decide separately whether to allow or disallow `GPTBot`.
+- Do not block OpenAI IP ranges in Cloudflare/Vercel/firewall rules.
+- Track `chatgpt.com`, `chat.openai.com`, and `r.openai.com` referrals where analytics exposes them.
+
+### Perplexity
+
+Perplexity should be treated as a citation-first search engine. Its docs say allowing `PerplexityBot` helps ensure a site appears in search results, and its help center says PerplexityBot will not index text content from sites that disallow it through robots.txt: https://docs.perplexity.ai/guides/bots and https://www.perplexity.ai/help-center/en/articles/10354969-how-does-perplexity-follow-robots-txt
+
+Recommendation:
+
+- Allow `PerplexityBot`.
+- Avoid pages where the answer is buried under long narrative intros.
+- Use tables, steps, FAQs, and concise definitions.
+- Cite official sources and show update dates.
+- Monitor `perplexity.ai` referrals and manually test priority prompts monthly.
+
+### Bing Copilot
+
+Copilot Search displays sources and links, and Microsoft 365 Copilot web search uses Bing-generated web queries when web search is on. For this site, Bing Webmaster Tools and IndexNow are the practical Copilot visibility path: https://www.microsoft.com/en-us/bing/copilot-search and https://support.microsoft.com/en-us/topic/how-web-search-works-in-microsoft-365-copilot-chat-and-agents-94c45d32-1a77-4f82-8e05-58dfb9afac48
+
+### Google AI Overviews and AI Mode
+
+Google says AI features are part of Search, and sites in AI features are included in overall Search Console traffic: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/appearance/ai-overviews
+
+Google's May 2025 AI Mode update shows the direction: deeper reasoning, multimodal search, and more complex query handling: https://blog.google/products-and-platforms/products/search/google-search-ai-mode-update/
+
+Recommendation:
+
+- Keep doing technical SEO and organic ranking work.
+- Create answer-first sections that can be cited.
+- Use structured data that matches the content.
+- Add original evidence that AI cannot get elsewhere.
+- Track AI Overview presence with third-party tools or manual prompt sets because Search Console does not expose a complete standalone AI Overview report.
+
+### How to Become Citable in AI Search
+
+AI-search citation research is still developing, but several patterns are consistent:
+
+- Ahrefs found AI assistants cite/reference URLs that often do not overlap with Google's top 10, so normal organic ranking is not the whole game: https://ahrefs.com/blog/ai-search-overlap/
+- Yext analyzed millions of AI citations and found first-party websites and brand-managed sources were major citation sources: https://www.yext.com/about/news-media/ai-citations-release
+- The GEO paper and later GEO research found that adding statistics, citations, authoritative wording, and structured evidence can improve visibility in generated answers: https://arxiv.org/abs/2311.09735 and https://arxiv.org/abs/2603.29979
+- A 2025 arXiv study of news-source citation patterns across OpenAI, Perplexity, and Google found different providers cite different sources, so cross-engine visibility needs cross-engine testing: https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.05301
+- A 2026 arXiv framework splits AI search optimization into citation selection and citation absorption, which is useful operationally: first get selected, then make sure the answer actually uses your evidence: https://arxiv.org/abs/2604.25707
+
+Content pattern for this China-travel site:
+
+```text
+Direct answer: Can foreigners use Alipay in China in 2026?
+
+Short answer: Yes, most foreign visitors can use Alipay by downloading the international app, verifying identity when prompted, and binding an eligible foreign bank card. Acceptance and limits vary by merchant, card issuer, and risk checks. Last checked: YYYY-MM-DD.
+
+Then include:
+- supported card networks;
+- exact setup steps;
+- screenshots;
+- known failure cases;
+- official Alipay/help links;
+- alternatives: WeChat Pay, cash, bank ATM, hotel front desk;
+- city-specific notes;
+- FAQ;
+- schema;
+- translated versions.
+```
+
+## H. International Targeting
+
+### Recommended URL and hreflang Structure
+
+Use one strong domain with language subdirectories:
+
+| Language | URL prefix | hreflang |
+|---|---:|---:|
+| English | `/en/` | `en` |
+| Simplified Chinese | `/zh-hans/` | `zh-Hans` |
+| Spanish | `/es/` | `es` |
+| French | `/fr/` | `fr` |
+| German | `/de/` | `de` |
+| Japanese | `/ja/` | `ja` |
+| Korean | `/ko/` | `ko` |
+| Russian | `/ru/` | `ru` |
+| Default selector | `/` or `/en/` depending UX | `x-default` |
+
+Example for one page:
+
+```html
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="en" href="https://example.com/en/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="zh-Hans" href="https://example.com/zh-hans/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="es" href="https://example.com/es/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="fr" href="https://example.com/fr/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="de" href="https://example.com/de/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="ja" href="https://example.com/ja/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="ko" href="https://example.com/ko/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="ru" href="https://example.com/ru/alipay-for-foreigners/" />
+<link rel="alternate" hreflang="x-default" href="https://example.com/" />
+```
+
+Implementation rules:
+
+- Put the full reciprocal set on every language version.
+- Include self-reference.
+- Use absolute URLs.
+- Keep canonical language-specific.
+- Keep language switcher crawlable with normal `<a href>`.
+- Do not block language versions in robots.txt.
+- Do not redirect Googlebot/Bingbot/YandexBot/Yeti/Baiduspider/OAI-SearchBot by IP or `Accept-Language`.
+
+Google hreflang reference: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/advanced/crawling/localized-versions
+
+### ccTLDs vs Subdirectories vs Subdomains
+
+Recommendation for this site: use subdirectories.
+
+| Option | Pros | Cons | Recommendation |
+|---|---|---|---|
+| ccTLDs, e.g. `example.kr`, `example.ru` | Strong local signal, local trust | Expensive, fragmented authority, more ops, legal/domain constraints | Avoid at launch |
+| Subdomains, e.g. `ko.example.com` | Can isolate stacks/teams | Weaker shared authority, more analytics/ops complexity | Use only if forced by platform |
+| Subdirectories, e.g. `example.com/ko/` | Shared authority, easiest ops, easiest internal links and analytics | Less explicit country signal than ccTLD | Best launch choice |
+| URL parameters | Easy technically | Weak crawlability and targeting clarity | Avoid |
+
+Google multi-regional docs: https://developers.google.com/search/docs/advanced/crawling/managing-multi-regional-sites
+
+### Hosting Location
+
+For global SEO, hosting location matters less than crawlability, speed, and availability. Google's multi-regional documentation notes server location is not a clear signal because CDNs are common. For Bing, location/language can be considered, but page language and user relevance matter more in practice.
+
+Practical recommendation:
+
+- Host on a reliable global edge platform.
+- Keep TTFB low in North America, Europe, Korea, Japan, Southeast Asia, and Australia.
+- Use image optimization and static caching heavily.
+- Use Hong Kong, Singapore, Tokyo, Seoul, and US/EU edge coverage for traveler markets.
+- Treat mainland China as a separate infrastructure project because of ICP and network constraints.
+
+### Cloudflare vs Vercel Edge
+
+Both can work.
+
+Use Vercel Edge if:
+
+- the app is Next.js or static frontend-heavy;
+- the team wants simple deploy previews and edge caching;
+- most users are outside mainland China;
+- engineering speed matters more than advanced network controls.
+
+Vercel CDN docs say Vercel has a globally distributed CDN and edge network: https://vercel.com/docs/cdn and https://vercel.com/docs/edge-network/regions
+
+Important China note: Vercel says it has no mainland China infrastructure and China network controls may block or throttle traffic to foreign domains, including `.vercel.app` subdomains: https://vercel.com/kb/guide/accessing-vercel-hosted-sites-from-mainland-china
+
+Use Cloudflare if:
+
+- the team wants stronger DNS/WAF/cache control;
+- bot access and AI crawler controls need explicit management;
+- you want to inspect and manage OpenAI/Perplexity/other crawler behavior;
+- you want operational control in front of another host.
+
+Cloudflare AI crawler references include `OAI-SearchBot`, `GPTBot`, and `PerplexityBot`: https://developers.cloudflare.com/ai-crawl-control/reference/bots/
+
+Avoid accidental AI-search invisibility:
+
+- If using Cloudflare bot controls, explicitly allow search and AI-search crawlers you want: Googlebot, Bingbot, DuckDuckBot, YandexBot, Yeti, Baiduspider, OAI-SearchBot, PerplexityBot.
+- If blocking training crawlers, separate that from search crawlers. Blocking `GPTBot` is not the same as blocking `OAI-SearchBot`.
+
+## I. Concrete Checklist
+
+### Day-1
+
+1. Day-1: Choose one canonical domain and subdirectory language architecture: `/en/`, `/zh-hans/`, `/es/`, `/fr/`, `/de/`, `/ja/`, `/ko/`, `/ru/`.
+2. Day-1: Create crawlable sitemap index plus per-language sitemaps with accurate `lastmod`.
+3. Day-1: Create robots.txt with sitemap reference and explicit access for major crawlers: Googlebot, Bingbot, DuckDuckBot, YandexBot, Naver Yeti, Baiduspider, OAI-SearchBot, PerplexityBot.
+4. Day-1: Set up Google Search Console and Bing Webmaster Tools.
+5. Day-1: Implement IndexNow key and API pipeline for changed URLs.
+6. Day-1: Add server log or edge-log retention for crawler diagnostics.
+7. Day-1: Define 30-50 priority travel problem pages, not generic destination listicles.
+8. Day-1: Build page templates with answer-first summary, update date, source citations, FAQ block, table support, breadcrumb, author/reviewer, and language switcher.
+9. Day-1: Decide AI crawler policy: allow `OAI-SearchBot` and `PerplexityBot`; separately decide on `GPTBot`.
+
+### Pre-launch
+
+10. Pre-launch: Publish English core pages for visa-free transit, payment apps, SIM/eSIM, VPN/access expectations, train tickets, metro, ride hailing, hotel check-in, emergency help, and top city arrival guides.
+11. Pre-launch: Add `hreflang` reciprocal tags and self-referencing canonicals across all launched languages.
+12. Pre-launch: Add structured data where it matches the page: `Article`, `FAQPage` where appropriate, `BreadcrumbList`, `HowTo` for procedural pages, and `Organization`/`WebSite`.
+13. Pre-launch: Compress and resize images; use descriptive filenames and alt text with English plus local place names where relevant.
+14. Pre-launch: Pass Core Web Vitals lab checks and manually test mobile interaction latency on route/payment/FAQ pages.
+15. Pre-launch: Submit sitemap index in Google and Bing.
+16. Pre-launch: Use Google URL Inspection and Bing URL Inspection on homepage plus 10 critical pages.
+17. Pre-launch: Add Yandex Webmaster and submit sitemap if `/ru/` exists.
+18. Pre-launch: Add Naver Search Advisor and submit sitemap if `/ko/` exists.
+19. Pre-launch: Create Korean Naver Blog seed content for 5-10 high-intent Korean travel problems and link naturally to the Korean evergreen pages.
+20. Pre-launch: Create Russian native pages for the most volatile/high-intent topics, with official-source citations and Cyrillic query coverage.
+21. Pre-launch: Prepare analytics segments for Google, Bing, Yandex, Naver, DuckDuckGo, ChatGPT, Perplexity, Copilot, and referral domains.
+22. Pre-launch: Manually test rendering without JavaScript for the main article content and links.
+
+### Post-launch
+
+23. Post-launch: Submit new/changed URLs with IndexNow after every publish/update/delete.
+24. Post-launch: Review Google Search Console and Bing Webmaster Tools weekly for indexing gaps, query mismatches, crawl errors, and top pages by country.
+25. Post-launch: Run monthly manual AI-search tests for 30 prompts across ChatGPT Search, Perplexity, Bing Copilot, and Google AI Overviews/AI Mode; record cited URLs.
+26. Post-launch: Update volatile pages monthly or whenever policies change; keep visible "last checked" dates.
+27. Post-launch: Build authority through useful external mentions: travel forums, Reddit where allowed, Korean Naver Blog/Cafe, Russian travel media/forums, YouTube descriptions, embassy/expat resources, and partner travel sites.
+28. Post-launch: Expand language coverage based on measured demand, starting with Korean and Russian if resources are constrained.
+29. Post-launch: Consider Baidu registration only after a maintained Simplified Chinese content set exists and there is evidence of China-internal or Chinese-language demand.
+30. Post-launch: Add original data assets that AI engines need to cite: foreign-card acceptance tables, airport-transfer comparisons, city-by-city payment failure notes, attraction booking requirements, and date-stamped screenshots.
+
